Golden Enterprises
 Inc. (the &#8220;Company&#8221;) is a holding company which owns all of the issued and outstanding capital stock of Golden Flake Snack Foods
 Inc.
 a wholly-owned operating subsidiary company (&#8220;Golden Flake&#8221; or the &#8220;Company&#8221;).


The Company was originally organized under the laws of the State of Alabama as Magic City Food Products
 Inc. on June 11
 1946.&#160;&#160;On March 11
 1958
 it adopted the name Golden Flake
 Inc.&#160;&#160;&#160;The Company was reorganized December 31
 1967 as a Delaware corporation.&#160;&#160;On January 1
 1977
 the Company
 which had been engaged in the business of manufacturing and distributing potato chips
 fried pork skins
 cheese curls
 and other snack foods
 spun off its operating division into a separate Delaware corporation known as Golden Flake Snack Foods
 Inc. and adopted its present name of Golden Enterprises
 Inc.


Golden Flake Snack Foods
 Inc.





Golden Flake is a Delaware corporation with its principal place of business and home office located at One Golden Flake Drive
 Birmingham
 Alabama.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake has been a premiere producer
 marketer
 and distributor of snack products in the Southeastern United States since 1923.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake manufactures and distributes a full line of high quality salted snack items
 such as potato chips
 tortilla chips
 corn chips
 fried pork skins
 baked and fried cheese curls
 onion rings
 and puff corn.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake also sells canned dips
 pretzels
 peanut butter crackers
 cheese crackers
 dried meat products
 and nuts packaged by other manufacturers using the Golden Flake label.




Golden Flake purchases raw materials used in manufacturing and processing its snack food products from various sources.&#160;&#160;A large part of the raw materials used by Golden Flake consists of farm commodities
 most notably corn
 potatoes and pork skin pellets
 which are subject to precipitous change in supply and price.&#160;&#160;Weather varies from season to season and directly affects both the quality and quantity of supply available.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake has no control over the agricultural aspects or prices and its profits are affected accordingly.&#160;&#160;The Company also purchases flexible bags or other suitable wrapping material for the storage
 shipment
 and presentation of the finished product to the customers.





Golden Flake sells its products through both its own sales organization and independent distributors
 principally to commercial establishments which sell food products in Alabama
 Tennessee
 Georgia
 Mississippi
 Louisiana
 Kentucky
 and South Carolina as well as parts of Florida
 North Carolina
 Arkansas
 Missouri
 Oklahoma
 Virginia
 Indiana
 and Texas.&#160;&#160;The Golden Flake brand is well-known throughout the Southeast.&#160;&#160;The products are distributed to its sales organization and independent distributors by either company transportation or commercial carrier out of the Birmingham and Ocala plants.


Golden Flake&#8217;s products are sold to a wide variety of grocery store chains
 discount stores
 convenience stores
 restaurants
 and other outlets located in our marketing area.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake is not dependent on any one or a few major customers.




















The snack foods business is highly competitive.&#160;&#160;In the area in which Golden Flake operates
 many companies engage in the production and distribution of food products similar to those produced and sold by Golden Flake.&#160;&#160;Most
 if not all
 of Golden Flake&#8217;s products are in direct competition with similar products of several local and regional companies
 many of which are larger in terms of capital and sales volume than is Golden Flake
 and at least one national company
 the Frito Lay Division of Pepsi Co.
 Inc..&#160;&#160;Golden Flake&#8217;s marketing thrust is aimed at selling the highest quality product possible and giving good service to its customers
 while being competitive with its prices.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake constantly tests the quality of its products for comparison with other similar products of competitors and maintains tight quality controls over its products.&#160;&#160;The Company believes that one of its major advantages is the Golden Flake brand
 which has been developed and enhanced throughout the history of the company and is now well known within the geographic area served by the Company.&#160;&#160;The Company continues to promote the Golden Flake brand through sponsorship agreements
 billboard campaigns
 advertising
 and other efforts.





The name &#8220;Golden Flake&#8221; and its regularly used symbol are federally registered trademarks of the Company.&#160;&#160;The Company also owns other trademarks such as &#8220;The South&#8217;s Original Potato Chip&#8221;
 a Golden Flake design from 1922
 the name &#8220;Sweetheat&#8221; and certain other trademarks not used on a regular basis.





As of June 12
 2015
 Golden Flake employed approximately 744 employees.&#160;&#160;Of these employees
 725 were full-time
 while 19 were part-time.&#160;&#160;Approximately 311 employees are involved in sales
 199 are in production
 133 are in management and 101 are in administrative personnel.


Golden Flake believes that the performance and loyalty of its employees are two of the most important factors in the growth and profitability of its business.&#160;&#160;Since labor costs represent a significant portion of Golden Flake&#8217;s expenses
 employee productivity is important to profitability.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake considers all of its employees to be a part of the &#8220;Golden Flake Family&#8221;.





The Company&#8217;s Annual Report on Form 10-K
 Quarterly Reports on Form 10-Q
 and other filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission can be found at the Company&#8217;s website located at 
 under the financial tab.

 and his present terms of office will expire on June 3

As a smaller reporting company
 the Company is not required to provide a statement of risk factors.&#160;&#160;However
 the Company believes this information may be valuable to our shareholders for this filing.&#160;&#160;The Company reserves the right to not provide risk factors in the future.


Important factors that could cause the Company&#8217;s actual business results
 performance
 or achievements to differ materially from any forward looking statements or other projections contained in this Annual Form 10-K Report include
 but are not limited to the principal risk factors set forth below.&#160;&#160;Additional risks and uncertainties
 including risks not presently known to the Company
 or that it currently deems immaterial
 may also impair the Company&#8217;s business and or operations. If the events discussed in these risk factors occur
 the Company&#8217;s business
 financial condition
 results of operations or cash flow could be adversely affected in a material way and the market value of the Company&#8217;s common stock could decline.





Price competition and consolidation within the Snack Food industry could adversely impact the Company&#8217;s performance.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s business requires significant marketing and sales effort to compete with larger companies.&#160;&#160;These larger competitors sell a significant portion of their products through discounting and other price cutting techniques.&#160;&#160;This intense competition increases the possibility that the Company could lose one or more customers
 lose market share and/or be forced to increase discounts
 and reduce pricing
 any of which could have an adverse impact on the Company&#8217;s business
 financial condition
 results of operation
 and/or cash flow.





Significant commodity price fluctuations for certain commodities purchased by the Company
 particularly potatoes
 corn
 pork skins
 and cooking oils could have a material impact on results of operations.&#160;&#160;These price fluctuations can be impacted by various factors including weather conditions
 such as flooding or drought.&#160;&#160;In an attempt to manage commodity cost fluctuations
 the Company
 in the normal course of business
 enters into contracts to purchase pre-established quantities of various types of raw materials
 at contracted prices based on expected short term needs.





The Company can be adversely impacted by changes in the cost of natural gas and other fuel costs
 such as gasoline and diesel fuel.&#160;&#160;Long term increases in the cost of natural gas and fuel costs could adversely impact and increase the Company&#8217;s cost of sales and marketing
 selling
 and delivery expenses.





Company operations use and store sensitive data
 including proprietary business information and personally identifiable information
 in secure data centers and on our networks. The Company could face a number of threats to its data centers and networks of unauthorized access
 security breaches and other system disruptions. It is critical to the Company that its infrastructure remains secure and is perceived by customers to be secure. The Company uses encryption and authentication technologies to secure the transmission and storage of data. Despite its security measures
 information technology systems may be vulnerable to attacks by hackers or other disruptive problems. Any such security breach may compromise information used or stored on the Company&#8217;s networks and may result in significant data losses or theft of our or our customers' proprietary business information or personally identifiable information. A cybersecurity breach could negatively affect the Company&#8217;s reputation. In addition
 a cyber attack could result in other negative consequences
 including remediation costs
 disruption of internal operations
 increased cybersecurity protection costs
 lost revenues or litigation
 which could have a material adverse effect on the business
 results of operations and financial condition of the Company.



















The Company is subject to a risk of product liability if the Company&#8217;s products actually are alleged to result
 in bodily injury. While the Company maintains what it believes to be reasonable limits of stop loss insurance coverage to appropriately respond to such liability exposures
 large product liability claims
 if made
 could exceed our insurance coverage limits. There can be no assurance that the Company will not incur significant costs in relation to such claims in the future.





The trading price of shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock may be affected by many factors and the price of shares of its common stock could decline.&#160;&#160;As a smaller publicly traded company
 the trading price of the Company&#8217;s common stock has fluctuated significantly in the past. The future trading price of the Company&#8217;s common stock may be volatile and could be subject to material price fluctuations.&#160;&#160;There are other risks and factors not described above that could also cause actual results to differ materially from those in any forward looking statement made by the Company.











The headquarters of the Company are located in Birmingham
 Alabama at One Golden Flake Drive.&#160;&#160;The properties of Golden Flake are described below.





The main plant and office headquarters of Golden Flake are located in Birmingham
 Alabama
 at One Golden Flake Drive and are situated on approximately 40 acres of land.&#160;&#160;This facility consists of three buildings which have a total of approximately 300
000 square feet of floor area.&#160;&#160;The Birmingham plant manufactures a full line of Golden Flake products.&#160;&#160;Golden Flake also has a garage and vehicle maintenance service center
 from which it services
 maintains
 repairs
 and rebuilds its fleet and delivery trucks in Birmingham.


Golden Flake also has a manufacturing plant in Ocala
 Florida.&#160;&#160;This plant was placed in service in November 1984.&#160;&#160;The Ocala plant consists of approximately 100
000 square feet of floor area and is located on a 28-acre site on Silver Springs Boulevard.&#160;&#160;The Company manufactures tortilla chips and potato chips from this facility.


Management believes that the Company&#8217;s facilities for the production of the products are suitable and adequate
 that they are being appropriately utilized in line with past experience
 and that they have sufficient production capacity for their present intended purposes.&#160;&#160;The extent of utilization of such facilities varies based upon seasonal demand for the products.&#160;&#160;It is not possible to measure with any degree of certainty or uniformity the productive capacity and extent of utilization of these facilities.&#160;&#160;However
 management believes that additional production can be obtained at the existing facilities by adding personnel and capital equipment
 by adding shifts of personnel
 or expanding the facilities.&#160;&#160;The Company continuously reviews our anticipated requirements for facilities and
 on the basis of that review
 may from time to time acquire additional facilities and/or dispose of existing facilities.























Golden Flake owns central branch warehouses in Birmingham
 Montgomery
 Midfield
 Demopolis
 Fort Payne
 Muscle Shoals
 Huntsville
 Phenix City
 Tuscaloosa
 Mobile
 Dothan
 and Oxford
 Alabama; Biloxi and Jackson
 Mississippi; Knoxville and Memphis
 Tennessee; Macon
 Georgia; Panama City
 Tallahassee
 and Pensacola
 Florida; and New Orleans
 Louisiana.&#160;&#160;The warehouses vary in size from 2
400 to 8
000 square feet.&#160;&#160;All central branch warehouses are owned free and clear of any debts.&#160;&#160;The Company also rents satellite warehouse branches throughout its distribution area.

GOLDEN ENTERPRISES
 INC. AND SUBSIDIARY






The following discussion provides an assessment of the Company&#8217;s financial condition
 results of operations
 liquidity
 and capital resources and should be read in conjunction with the accompanying consolidated financial statements and notes.





The Company manufactures and distributes a full line of snack items
 such as potato chips
 tortilla chips
 corn chips
 fried pork skins
 baked and fried cheese curls
 onion rings
 and puff corn.&#160;&#160;The products are all packaged in flexible bags or other suitable wrapping material.&#160;&#160;The Company also sells canned dips
 pretzels
 peanut butter crackers
 cheese crackers
 dried meat products
 and nuts packaged by other manufacturers using the Golden Flake label.


No single product or product line accounts for more than 50% of the Company&#8217;s sales
 which affords some protection against loss of volume due to a crop failure of major agricultural raw materials or failure to procure an adequate supply of pork skin pellets.&#160;&#160;Raw materials used in manufacturing and processing the Company&#8217;s snack food products are purchased on the open market
 under contract through brokers and directly from growers.&#160;&#160;A large part of the raw materials used by the Company consists of farm commodities which are subject to precipitous changes in supply and price.&#160;&#160;Weather varies from season to season and directly affects both the quality and supply of farm commodities available.&#160;&#160;The Company has no control of the agricultural aspects and its profits are affected accordingly.








The Company&#8217;s discussion and analysis of its financial condition and results of operations are based upon the Company&#8217;s consolidated financial statements
 the preparation of which is in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America which requires management to make estimates and assumptions that in certain circumstances affect amounts reported in the consolidated financial statements.&#160;&#160;In preparing these financial statements
 management has made its best estimates and judgments of certain amounts included in the financial statements
 giving due considerations to materiality.&#160;&#160;The Company does not believe there is a great likelihood that materially different amounts would be reported under different conditions or using different assumptions related to the accounting policies described below.&#160;&#160;However
 application of these accounting policies involves the exercise of judgment and use of assumptions as to future uncertainties and
 as a result
 actual results could differ materially from these estimates.&#160;&#160;Other accounting policies and estimates are detailed in Note 1 of the Notes To Consolidated Financial Statements in this Form 10-K.





















The Company recognizes sales and related costs upon delivery or shipment of products to its customers
 including independent distributors.&#160;&#160;Sales are reduced by returns from and allowances to customers.





The Company records accounts receivable at the time revenue is recognized.&#160;&#160;Amounts for bad debt expense are recorded in selling
 general and administrative expenses on the Consolidated Statements of Operations.&#160;&#160;The amount of the allowance for doubtful accounts is based on management&#8217;s estimate of the accounts receivable amount that is uncollectible.&#160;&#160;The Company records a general reserve based on analysis of historical data.&#160;&#160;In addition
 the Company records specific reserves for receivable balances that are considered high-risk due to known facts regarding the customer.&#160;&#160;The allowance for bad debts is reviewed quarterly
 and determined whether the amount should be changed.&#160;&#160;Failure of a major customer to pay the Company amounts owed could have a material impact on the financial statements of the Company. At May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014
 the Company had accounts receivables in the amount of $11
085
689 and $11
341
024
 net of an allowance for doubtful accounts of $70
000 and $70
000
 respectively.&#160;&#160;The Company did not have any major customer write-offs this year that were not covered by credit insurance.





Inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market.&#160;&#160;Cost is computed on the first-in
 first out method.





The Company is self-insured for certain casualty losses relating to automobile liability
 general liability
 workers&#8217; compensation
 property losses
 and medical claims all of which are herein referred to as &#8220;Casualty Expenses&#8221;.&#160;&#160;Management estimates certain expenses in an effort to record those expenses in the period incurred. The Company&#8217;s significant estimates relate to Casualty Expenses.&#160;&#160;The Company also has stop loss insurance coverage to limit the exposure arising from these claims.&#160;&#160;Automobile liability
 general liability
 workers&#8217; compensation
 and property losses costs are covered by letters of credit with the company&#8217;s claim administrators.





In determining the ultimate loss and reserve requirements
 the third-party actuary uses various actuarial assumptions including compensation trends
 health care cost trends
 and discount rates. The third-party actuary also uses historical information for claims frequency and severity in order to establish loss development factors.


The actuarial calculation includes a factor to account for changes in inflation
 health care costs
 compensation and litigation cost trends
 as well as estimated future incurred claims.&#160;&#160;This year
 the Company utilized a 50% confidence level for estimating the ultimate outstanding casualty liability based on the actuarial report.&#160;&#160;This assumes that approximately 50% of each claim should be equal to or less than the ultimate liability recorded based on the historical trends experienced by the Company.&#160;&#160;If the Company chose a 75% factor
 the liability would have been increased by approximately $0.3 million.&#160;&#160;If the Company chose a 90% factor
 the liability would have increased by approximately $0.6 million.
















This year the Company used a 4% investment rate to discount the estimated claims based on the historical payout pattern during 2015 and 2014.&#160;&#160;A one percentage point change in the discount rate would have impacted the liability by approximately $36
000.





As of May 29
 2015
 the Company&#8217;s casualty reserve was $1
472
182 and at May 30
 2014 the casualty reserve was $1
349
181.








The Company has a letter of credit in the amount of $1
850
000 outstanding at May 29
 2015 and $1
850
000 at May 30
 2014.&#160;&#160;The letter of credit supports the Company&#8217;s self-insurance program.


The Company has a line-of-credit agreement with a local bank that permits borrowing up to $3 million.&#160;&#160;The line-of-credit is subject to the Company&#8217;s continued credit worthiness and compliance with the terms and conditions of the loan agreement with the bank.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s line-of-credit debt at May 29
 2015 was $2
823
477 with an interest rate of 3.25%
 leaving the Company with $176
523 of credit availability.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s line-of-credit debt at May 30
 2014 was $2
528
511 with an interest rate of 3.25%
 leaving the Company with $471
489 of credit availability.


The Company&#8217;s current ratio (current assets divided by current liabilities) was 1.47 to 1.00 and 1.38 to 1.00 at May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014
 respectively.


Available cash
 cash from operations
 and available credit under the line of credit are expected to be sufficient to meet anticipated cash expenditures and normal operating requirements for the foreseeable future.








Cost of sales as a percentage of net sales amounted to 50.2% and 51.3% in 2015 and 2014
 respectively.


Selling
 general and administrative expenses were 47.4% of net sales in 2015 and 46.7% of net sales in 2014.


The Company&#8217;s effective tax rates for 2015 and 2014 were 42.2% and 42.2%
 respectively.&#160;&#160;Note 7 to the Consolidated Financial Statements provides additional information about the provision for income taxes.

The principal market risks (i.e. the risk of loss arising from adverse changes in market rates and prices) to which the Company is exposed are interest rates on its cash equivalents and bank loans
 fuel costs
 and commodity prices affecting the cost of its raw materials.


The Company is subject to market risk with respect to commodities because its ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which it operates.&#160;&#160;The Company purchases its raw materials on the open market
 under contract through brokers and directly from growers.&#160;&#160;Futures contracts have been used occasionally to hedge immaterial amounts of commodity purchases
 but none are presently being used.





Certain costs and expenses of the Company are affected by inflation. The Company&#8217;s prices for its products over the past several fiscal years have remained relatively flat. The Company plans to contend with the effect of further inflation through efficient purchasing
 improved manufacturing methods
 pricing
 and by monitoring and controlling expenses.

 and effectiveness of sales and marketing activities
 as described in this 10-K. You are cautioned not to place undue reliance on these forward-looking statements which speak only as of the date which they are made.

Golden Enterprises

We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and subsidiary (&#8220;the Company&#8221;) as of May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014
 and the related consolidated statements of income
 stockholders&#8217; equity
 and cash flows for the years then ended.&#160;&#160;Our audits also included the financial statement schedule of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and subsidiary listed in Item 15(a).&#160;&#160;These financial statements and financial statement schedule are the responsibility of the Company&#8217;s management.&#160;&#160;Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these consolidated financial statements and schedule based on our audits.


We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).&#160;&#160;Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement.&#160;&#160;The Company is not required to have
 nor were we engaged to perform
 an audit of its internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances
 but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#8217;s internal control over financial reporting.&#160;&#160;Accordingly
 we express no such opinion.&#160;&#160;An audit also includes examining
 on a test basis
 evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the consolidated financial statements
 assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management
 as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.&#160;&#160;We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.


In our opinion
 the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly
 in all material respects
 the financial position of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and subsidiary as of May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014
 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for the years then ended
 in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.&#160;&#160;Also
 in our opinion
 the&#160;&#160;financial statement schedule
 when considered in relation to the basic consolidated financial statements taken as a whole
 present fairly in all material respects the information set forth therein.

GOLDEN ENTERPRISES
 INC. AND SUBSIDIARY

For the Fiscal Years Ended May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014





The accounting and reporting policies of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and subsidiary (&#8220;Company&#8221;) conform to accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America and to general practices within the snack foods industry.&#160;&#160;The following is a description of the more significant accounting policies:







The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiary
 Golden Flake Snack Foods
 Inc.&#160;&#160;All significant inter-company transactions and balances have been eliminated.







The Company records accounts receivable at the time revenue is recognized.&#160;&#160;Amounts for bad debt expense are recorded in selling
 general and administrative expenses.&#160;&#160;The determination of the allowance for doubtful accounts is based on management&#8217;s estimate of uncollectible accounts receivables.&#160;&#160;The Company records a general reserve based on analysis of historical data.&#160;&#160;In addition
 management records specific reserves for receivable balances that are considered at higher risk due to known facts regarding the customer.



The Company ends its fiscal year on the Friday closest to the last day in May.&#160;&#160;The year ended May 29
 2015 included 52 weeks as did the year ended May 30
 2014.


The carrying amounts of cash and cash equivalents
 receivables
 accounts payable
 and short-term debt approximate fair value.







Inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market.&#160;&#160;Cost is computed on the first-in
 first-out method.


















GOLDEN ENTERPRISES
 INC. AND SUBSIDIARY

For the Fiscal Years Ended May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014


Property
 Plant and Equipment
Property
 plant and equipment are stated at cost.&#160;&#160;For financial reporting purposes
 depreciation and amortization have been provided principally on the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the respective assets.&#160;&#160;Accelerated methods are used for tax purposes. Expenditures for maintenance and repairs are charged to operations as incurred; expenditures for renewals and betterments are capitalized and written off by depreciation and amortization charges.&#160;&#160;Property retired or sold is removed from the asset and related accumulated depreciation accounts and any profit or loss resulting there from is reflected in the statements of operations.



The Company is self-insured for certain casualty losses relating to automobile liability
 general liability
 workers&#8217; compensation
 property losses
 and medical claims.&#160;&#160;The Company also has stop loss coverage to limit the exposure arising from these claims.&#160;&#160;Automobile liability
 general liability
 workers&#8217; compensation
 and property losses costs are covered by letters of credit with the company&#8217;s claim administrators.


Due to the complexity of estimating the timing and amounts of insurance claims
 the Company uses a third-party actuary to estimate the casualty insurance obligations on an annual basis.&#160;&#160;In determining the ultimate loss and reserve requirements
 the third-party uses various actuarial assumptions including compensation trends
 health care cost trends
 and discount rates. The third-party actuary also uses historical information for claims frequency and severity in order to establish loss development factors. The actuarial calculation includes a factor to account for changes in inflation
 health care costs
 compensation
 and litigation cost trends
 as well as estimated future incurred claims.&#160;&#160;Large fluctuations in claims can have a significant impact on selling
 general and administrative expenses.



The Company expenses advertising costs as incurred.&#160;&#160;These costs are included in selling
 general and administrative expenses.&#160;&#160;Advertising expense amounted to $7
973
958 and $7
767
596 for the fiscal years 2015 and 2014
 respectively.



Deferred income taxes are provided using the liability method to measure tax consequences resulting from differences between financial accounting standards and applicable income tax laws.&#160;&#160;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a valuation allowance when
 in the opinion of management
 it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not be realized.&#160;&#160;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates on the date of enactment.







The Company granted stock options to management on April 9
 2015.&#160;&#160;See Note 8 for further discussion of the Company&#8217;s stock option awards.


















GOLDEN ENTERPRISES
 INC. AND SUBSIDIARY

For the Fiscal Years Ended May 29

Shipping and handling costs
 which include salaries and vehicle operations expenses relating to the delivery of products to customers by the Company
 are classified as selling
 general and administrative expenses.&#160;&#160;Shipping and handling costs amounted to $3
827
583 and $3
838

 respectively.

The Company determined that there had been an error in its accounting for deferred income taxes. The error resulted in an understatement of deferred income tax assets
 and an understatement of deferred income tax liabilities. A restatement adjustment was made to correct the error by increasing deferred income tax assets $835
832
 and increasing deferred income tax liabilities by the same amount. The adjustments resulted in no change to the equity position of the Company or earnings per share.

 subject to the terms of the Plan

Basic earnings per common share are computed by dividing earnings available to stockholders by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.&#160;&#160;Diluted earnings per share reflects per share amounts that would have resulted if dilutive potential common stock equivalents had been converted to common stock
 as prescribed by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 128
 &#8220;Earnings per Share&#8221;. At May 29
 2015
 options on the 310
000 shares were included in the computation of diluted earnings per share because the options&#8217; exercise price was less than the average market price of the common shares and were therefore dilutive. The dilutive effect of stock options was calculated using the Treasury Stock method.&#160;&#160;The following reconciles the information used to compute basic and diluted earnings per share:

Fair value is defined as the quoted market prices for those instruments that are actively traded in financial markets.&#160;&#160;In cases where quoted market prices are not available
 fair values are estimated using present value or other valuation techniques.&#160;&#160;The fair value estimates are made at a specific point in time
 based on available market information and judgments about the financial instruments
 such as estimates of timing and amount of expected future cash flows.&#160;&#160;Such estimates do not reflect any premium or discount that could result from offering for sale at one time the Company&#8217;s entire holdings of a particular financial instrument
 nor do they consider the tax impact of the realization of unrealized gains or losses.&#160;&#160;In many cases
 the fair value estimates cannot be substantiated by comparison to independent markets
 nor can the disclosed value be realized in immediate settlement of the instrument.


The carrying amounts for cash and cash equivalents approximate fair value because of the short maturity
 generally less than three months
 of these instruments.

 2014.&#160;&#160;The letter of credit supports the Company&#8217;s commercial self-insurance program.&#160;&#160;The Company pays an annual commitment fee of 0.75% to maintain the letters of credit.





The Company is subject to routine litigation and claims incidental to its business.&#160;&#160;In the opinion of management
 such routine litigation and claims should not have a material adverse effect upon the Company&#8217;s consolidated financial statements taken as a whole.

The Company maintains deposit relationships with high credit quality financial institutions.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s trade receivables result primarily from its snack food operations and reflect a broad customer base
 primarily large grocery store chains located in the Southeastern United States.&#160;&#160;The Company routinely assesses the financial strength of its customers.&#160;&#160;As a consequence
 concentrations of credit risk are limited.

Our company&#8217;s management
 under the supervision of and with the participation of our chief executive officer and chief financial officer
 evaluated the effectiveness of our disclosure controls and procedures as of May 29
 2015. The term &#8220;disclosure controls and procedures
&#8221; as defined in Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e) under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (the &#8220;Exchange Act&#8221;)
 means controls and other procedures of a company that are designed to ensure that information required to be disclosed by a company in the reports that it files or submits under the Exchange Act is recorded
 processed
 summarized and reported
 within the time periods specified in the Securities and Exchange Commission&#8217;s rules and forms. Disclosure controls and procedures include
 without limitation
 controls and procedures designed to ensure that information required to be disclosed by a company in the reports that it files or submits under the Exchange Act is accumulated and communicated to the company&#8217;s management
 including its principal executive and principal financial officers
 as appropriate to allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure. Management recognizes that any controls and procedures
 no matter how well designed and operated
 can provide only reasonable assurance of achieving their objectives and management necessarily applies its judgment in evaluating the cost-benefit relationship of possible controls and procedures. Based on the evaluation of our disclosure controls and procedures as of May 29
 2015
 our chief executive officer and chief financial officer concluded that
 as of such date
 our disclosure controls and procedures were effective at the reasonable assurance level.




The management of the company is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting for the company. Internal control over financial reporting is defined in Rule 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) promulgated under the Exchange Act as a process designed by
 or under the supervision of
 the company&#8217;s principal executive and principal financial officers and effected by the company&#8217;s board of directors
 management and other personnel
 to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and includes those policies and procedures that:



&#160;&#160;&#160;Provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles
 and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and

&#160;&#160;&#160;Provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition
 use or disposition of the company&#8217;s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
















Because of its inherent limitations
 internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements. Projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions
 or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.


The company&#8217;s management assessed the effectiveness of the company&#8217;s internal control over financial reporting as of May 29
 2015. In making this assessment
 the company&#8217;s management used the criteria set forth by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in its Internal Control-Integrated Framework.

Based on management&#8217;s assessment
 it concluded that
 as of May 29
 2015
 the company&#8217;s internal control over financial reporting was effective based on those criteria set forth.






No change in our internal controls over financial reporting occurred during the fiscal quarter ended May 29
 2015 that has materially affected
to materially affect
 our internal control over financial reporting.

 Inc. and furnished to the Securities and Exchange Commission or its staff upon request.

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 13 - CONCENTRATIONS OF CREDIT RISK&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company&amp;#x2019;s financial instruments that are exposed to
 concentrations of credit risk consist primarily of cash equivalents
 and trade receivables.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company maintains deposit relationships with high credit quality
 financial institutions.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Company&amp;#x2019;s trade
 receivables result primarily from its snack food operations and
 reflect a broad customer base
 primarily large grocery store chains
 located in the Southeastern United States.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Company
 routinely assesses the financial strength of its
 customers.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;As a consequence
 concentrations of credit
 risk are limited.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company did not have any major customer write-offs this year that
 were not covered by credit insurance.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Stock Options&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company granted stock options to management on April 9
 2015.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;See Note 8 for further discussion of the
 Company&amp;#x2019;s stock option awards.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 9 &amp;#x2013; LONG-TERM INCENTIVE PLANS&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company has a long-term incentive plan currently in effect under
 which stock option grants may be issued.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;A total of
 310
000 stock options were granted to key employees on April 9
 2015.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;This Plan (the 2014 Plan) is administered by the
 Stock Option Committee of the Board of Directors
 which has sole
 discretion
 subject to the terms of the Plan
 to determine those
 employees
 including executive officers
 eligible to receive awards
 and the amount and type of such awards.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Stock Option
 Committee also has the authority to interpret the Plan and make all
 other determinations required in the administration
 thereof.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;All options outstanding at the end of 2015 are
 not exercisable until April 9
 2016.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 2014 Plan provides
 for
 among other things
 the granting of
 Incentive Stock Options as defined under the Internal Revenue
 Code.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Under the Plan
 grants of incentive stock options
 may be made to selected officers and employees
 with a term not
 exceeding ten years from the issue date and at a price not
 less&lt;/font&gt; &lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;than
 the fair market value of the Company&amp;#x2019;s stock at the date of
 grant. 310
000 stock option awards were granted under the 2015 Plan
 for the year ended May 29
 2015.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Seven
 hundred fifty thousand shares of the Company&amp;#x2019;s stock were
 authorized for issuance under this Plan.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The following
 is a summary of transactions:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 11 &amp;#x2013; DISCLOSURES ABOUT FAIR VALUE OF FINANCIAL
 INSTRUMENTS&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Fair
 value is defined as the quoted market prices for those instruments
 that are actively traded in financial markets.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;In cases
 where quoted market prices are not available
 fair values are
 estimated using present value or other valuation
 techniques.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The fair value estimates are made at a
 specific point in time
 based on available market information and
 judgments about the financial instruments
 such as estimates of
 timing and amount of expected future cash flows.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Such
 estimates do not reflect any premium or discount that could result
 from offering for sale at one time the Company&amp;#x2019;s entire
 holdings of a particular financial instrument
 nor do they consider
 the tax impact of the realization of unrealized gains or
 losses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;In many cases
 the fair value estimates cannot
 be substantiated by comparison to independent markets
 nor can the
 disclosed value be realized in immediate settlement of the
 instrument.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 carrying amounts for cash and cash equivalents approximate fair
 value because of the short maturity
 generally less than three
 months
 of these instruments.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 carrying value of the Company&amp;#x2019;s salary continuation plan and
 accrued liability approximates fair value because present value is
 used in accruing this liability.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company does not hold or issue financial instruments for trading
 purposes and has no involvement with forward currency exchange
 contracts.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;There
 were no new accounting pronouncements that were of significance or
 potential significance to us.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company considers all highly liquid investments purchased with a
 maturity of three months or less to be cash
 equivalents.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Income Taxes&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Deferred
 income taxes are provided using the liability method to measure tax
 consequences resulting from differences between financial
 accounting standards and applicable income tax
 laws.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a valuation
 allowance when
 in the opinion of management
 it is more likely
 than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will
 not be realized.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are
 adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates on the
 date of enactment.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Other
 long-term obligations at May 29

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;At
 May 29
 2015 and May 30
 2014 the provision for income taxes
 consists of the following:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;
 &lt;div align=left&gt;
 &lt;table style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 width=100%&gt;
 &lt;tr&gt;
 &lt;td style=PADDING-BOTTOM: 2px valign=bottom&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&amp;#xA0;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Revenue Recognition&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company recognizes sales and related costs upon delivery or
 shipment of products to its customers.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Sales are reduced
 by returns and allowances to customers.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Accounts Receivable&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company records accounts receivable at the time revenue is
 recognized.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Amounts for bad debt expense are recorded in
 selling
 general and administrative expenses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The
 determination of the allowance for doubtful accounts is based on
 management&amp;#x2019;s estimate of uncollectible accounts
 receivables.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Company records a general reserve based
 on analysis of historical data.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;In addition
 management
 records specific reserves for receivable balances that are
 considered at higher risk due to known facts regarding the
 customer.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 10 &amp;#x2013; NET INCOME PER SHARE&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Basic
 earnings per common share are computed by dividing earnings
 available to stockholders by the weighted average number of common
 shares outstanding during the period.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Diluted earnings
 per share reflects per share amounts that would have resulted if
 dilutive potential common stock equivalents had been converted to
 common stock
 as prescribed by Statement of Financial Accounting
 Standards No. 128
 &amp;#x201C;Earnings per Share&amp;#x201D;. At May 29
 2015
 options on the 310
000 shares were included in the
 computation of diluted earnings per share because the
 options&amp;#x2019; exercise price was less than the average market
 price of the common shares and were therefore dilutive. The
 dilutive effect of stock options was calculated using the Treasury
 Stock method.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The following reconciles the information
 used to compute basic and diluted earnings per share:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 Advertising&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 Company expenses advertising costs as incurred.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;These
 costs are included in selling
 general and administrative
 expenses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Advertising expense amounted to $7
973
958 and

767
596 for the fiscal years 2015 and 2014
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&amp;#xA0;&lt;/div&gt;

 tax effects of temporary differences that result in deferred tax

 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company and its subsidiary are subject to federal income tax as
 well as income tax of various states. The Company is no longer
 subject to examination for years before 2011.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;


 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 1 - SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING
 POLICIES&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 accounting and reporting policies of Golden Enterprises
 Inc. and
 subsidiary (&amp;#x201C;Company&amp;#x201D;) conform to accounting principles
 generally accepted in the United States of America and to general
 practices within the snack foods industry.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The following
 is a description of the more significant accounting
 policies:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Nature of the Business&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company manufactures and distributes a full line of snack items
 that are sold through its own sales organization and independent
 distributors to commercial establishments that sell food products
 primarily in the Southeastern United States.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Consolidation&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Golden
 Enterprises
 Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiary
 Golden Flake
 Snack Foods
 Inc.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;All significant inter-company
 transactions and balances have been eliminated.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Revenue Recognition&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company recognizes sales and related costs upon delivery or
 shipment of products to its customers.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Sales are reduced
 by returns and allowances to customers.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Accounts Receivable&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company records accounts receivable at the time revenue is
 recognized.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Amounts for bad debt expense are recorded in
 selling
 general and administrative expenses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The
 determination of the allowance for doubtful accounts is based on
 management&amp;#x2019;s estimate of uncollectible accounts
 receivables.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Company records a general reserve based
 on analysis of historical data.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;In addition
 management
 records specific reserves for receivable balances that are
 considered at higher risk due to known facts regarding the
 customer.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Fiscal Year&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company ends its fiscal year on the Friday closest to the last day
 in May.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The year ended May 29
 2015 included 52 weeks as
 did the year ended May 30
 2014.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
 &amp;#xA0;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 carrying amounts of cash and cash equivalents
 receivables
 accounts payable
 and short-term debt approximate fair
 value.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company considers all highly liquid investments purchased with a
 maturity of three months or less to be cash
 equivalents.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Inventories&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Inventories
 are stated at the lower of cost or market.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Cost is
 computed on the first-in
 first-out method.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Property
 Plant and Equipment&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Property
 plant and equipment are stated at cost.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;For financial
 reporting purposes
 depreciation and amortization have been
 provided principally on the straight-line method over the estimated
 useful lives of the respective assets.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Accelerated
 methods are used for tax purposes. Expenditures for maintenance and
 repairs are charged to operations as incurred; expenditures for
 renewals and betterments are capitalized and written off by
 depreciation and amortization charges.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Property retired
 or sold is removed from the asset and related accumulated
 depreciation accounts and any profit or loss resulting there from
 is reflected in the statements of operations.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Self-Insurance&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company is self-insured for certain casualty losses relating to
 automobile liability
 general liability
 workers&amp;#x2019;
 compensation
 property losses
 and medical claims.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The
 Company also has stop loss coverage to limit the exposure arising
 from these claims.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Automobile liability
 general
 liability
 workers&amp;#x2019; compensation
 and property losses costs
 are covered by letters of credit with the company&amp;#x2019;s claim
 administrators.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Due
 to the complexity of estimating the timing and amounts of insurance
 claims
 the Company uses a third-party actuary to estimate the
 casualty insurance obligations on an annual basis.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;In
 determining the ultimate loss and reserve requirements
 the
 third-party uses various actuarial assumptions including
 compensation trends
 health care cost trends
 and discount rates.
 The third-party actuary also uses historical information for claims
 frequency and severity in order to establish loss development
 factors. The actuarial calculation includes a factor to account for
 changes in inflation
 health care costs
 compensation
 and
 litigation cost trends
 as well as estimated future incurred
 claims.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Large fluctuations in claims can have a
 significant impact on selling
 general and administrative
 expenses.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Advertising&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company expenses advertising costs as incurred.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;These
 costs are included in selling
 general and administrative
 expenses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Advertising expense amounted to $7
973
958 and
 $7
767
596 for the fiscal years 2015 and 2014
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Income Taxes&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Deferred
 income taxes are provided using the liability method to measure tax
 consequences resulting from differences between financial
 accounting standards and applicable income tax
 laws.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a valuation
 allowance when
 in the opinion of management
 it is more likely
 than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will
 not be realized.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are
 adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates on the
 date of enactment.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Segment Information&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company does not identify separate operating segments for
 management reporting purposes.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The results of operations
 are the basis on which management evaluates operations and makes
 business decisions.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;The Company&amp;#x2019;s sales are
 generated primarily within the Southeastern United
 States.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Stock Options&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company granted stock options to management on April 9
 2015.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;See Note 8 for further discussion of the
 Company&amp;#x2019;s stock option awards.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Shipping and Handling Costs&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Shipping
 and handling costs
 which include salaries and vehicle operations
 expenses relating to the delivery of products to customers by the
 Company
 are classified as selling
 general and administrative
 expenses.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Shipping and handling costs amounted to
 $3
827
583 and $3
838
605 for the fiscal years 2015 and 2014
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Use of Estimates&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally
 accepted accounting principles requires management to make
 estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of
 assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and
 liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the
 reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting
 period.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Actual results could differ from those
 estimates.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;There
 were no new accounting pronouncements that were of significance or
 potential significance to us.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 restatement adjustments resulted in a change to the Company&amp;#x2019;s

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 2 &amp;#x2013; RESTATEMENT OF PRIOR PERIOD FINANCIAL
 STATEMENTS&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Prior
 period financial statements have been restated to reflect
 adjustments to the Company&amp;#x2019;s financial information previously
 reported on form 10K for the year ended May 30
 2014.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 Company determined that there had been an error in its accounting
 for deferred income taxes. The error resulted in an understatement
 of deferred income tax assets
 and an understatement of deferred
 income tax liabilities. A restatement adjustment was made to
 correct the error by increasing deferred income tax assets
 $835
832
 and increasing deferred income tax liabilities by the
 same amount. The adjustments resulted in no change to the equity
 position of the Company or earnings per share.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=left&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;These
 restatement adjustments resulted in a change to the Company&amp;#x2019;s
 working capital and current ratio calculations as
 follows:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=TEXT-ALIGN: left; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt&gt;

 &lt;td valign=bottom width=1%&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&amp;#xA0;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
 &lt;td valign=bottom width=40% colspan=6&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=center&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;May
 30

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Use of Estimates&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;The
 preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally
 accepted accounting principles requires management to make
 estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of
 assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and
 liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the
 reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting
 period.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Actual results could differ from those
 estimates.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

  

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 NOTE 12&amp;#x2013; COMMITMENTS AND CONTINGENCIES&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;&lt;font style=TEXT-DECORATION: underline; DISPLAY: inline&gt;
 Property
 Plant and Equipment&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
 &lt;div style=MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt align=justify&gt;&lt;font style=FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman; DISPLAY: inline&gt;Property
 plant and equipment are stated at cost.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;For financial
 reporting purposes
 depreciation and amortization have been
 provided principally on the straight-line method over the estimated
 useful lives of the respective assets.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Accelerated
 methods are used for tax purposes. Expenditures for maintenance and
 repairs are charged to operations as incurred; expenditures for
 renewals and betterments are capitalized and written off by
 depreciation and amortization charges.&amp;#xA0;&amp;#xA0;Property retired
 or sold is removed from the asset and related accumulated
 depreciation accounts and any profit or loss resulting there from
 is reflected in the statements of operations.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
